meanings: ['(1) **presentative particle** | in association with verbs of perception: *ʾə́θyela xə̀zyeˈ ʾína ṭéna kúlle ṃə́ḷya šə̀xtaˈ* They came and saw that the saddle bag was completely full of filth (A7:11); *qímela zíle xə́zye ʾína dū̀sˈ* They went and saw that it was true (A14:13); *xazéle ʾína bɛ́θe ṃə̀ḷyaˈ* He sees that his house is full (A21:8); *paθə̀xle tắra,ˈ ʾína xazéle ʾo-ʾažvána tàmaˈ* He opened the door and saw the caretaker there (A22:43). Implied verb of perception: *mátti bála gu-yàma,ˈ ʾìnaˈ ʾa-sústət yamàθaˈ nabòləllaˈ Čəlkằzeˈ* They looked at the sea (and saw) the mare of the seas taking away *Čəlkăze* (A12:34); *ʾo-xabúša pθìxtəlle,ˈ ʾína ʾisə́qθa dìyaˈ* She opened up the apple and (saw) her ring (A4:19). Introducing preliminary background material: *ṭḷáθna hon-yíwtəlla mòʿəd.ˈ ʾína ṱ-áθi làxxa.ˈ ʾáti kúl fàtraˈ mṭašə́tla gánux baràyeˈ* I have made an assignation with the three of them. Now, (when) they come here, each time you hide yourself outside (A22:21-22). Climactic result: *ṣléla tàma.ˈ ʾína kúlla gɛ́rme díya šmìṭe.ˈ* She went down there and all her bones were broken (A20:4). In commands: *ʾína m-báθər maqðàliˈ ʾaw-qə̀ṭmaˈ šaqlìtuleˈ mxamìtuleˈ* Now, after she burns me, take the ashes and keep them (A26:85).', '(2) **but** | drawing attention to something unexpected: *ʾána bắyənwa šaqlə́nwali xáčča mə̀šxaˈ ... ta-ṱ-áxlən b-ʾùrxaˈ xáčča mə́šxa-w lə̀xmaˈ ʾína ʾíði ṣéla gu-d-áwwa hə́nna lìntaˈ* I wanted to take a little oil to eat on the way, a little oil and bread, but my hand has got stuck in this thing, the pot (A23:8); *ʾə̀θyela,ˈ plíṭe bárqul mðitèy.ˈ ʾína mðitéy kúlla mxíθa l-kòmaˈ* They came out opposite their town. But, their town was all covered in black. (A4:28). In exclamatory constructions: *ʾánna ṣàliˈ ʾína mò ṣáliˈ* They went and what (a surprise when) they went down! (A25:13); *xá-bena plíṭṭɛla xa-bràta.ˈ ʾína mù-brata!ˈ* Then a girl came out, but what a girl! (A13:11); *xílənna ʾína mòdi!ˈ* I have eaten it, so what! (A2:11).', '(3) **otherwise** | *ʾána hon-márəllux b-àyya šárṭ ʾaláha t-yawə́llux,ˈ ʾína là-yawəlluxˈ* I am telling you, God will give to you on this condition, otherwise he will not give to you (A3:5).']

Only I have escaped (B19:8); *bas-mìya máttət qam-réša díyaˈ* Place only water by her head (A21:37); *bas-ʾɛ́ni t-xzéla ʾày xoš-ʾáza gu-jahànnamˈ* Only my eye, which saw it—let that go to Hell (A16:2); *ʾánna júlle dìye xə́zye básˈ* We only found these clothes of his (A14:17).', '(2) **no more** |. *mattátla xa-kawázət míya kəs-réša-w bàsˈ* Put out for her a jar of water by her head and no more (A21:10).', '(3) **if only** | Clausal connective: *xuš-mɛ̀θənˈ bas-xáθi Nozáli xazə̀nwalaˈ* Let me die, if only I could see my sister Nozali (A8:57).', '(4) **only if** | *bas-ʾánna xonăwáθi bàsmi,ˈ gorànnuxˈ* Only if you cure these brothers of mine, shall I marry you (A34:22).', '(5) **but** | Clausal connective: *ʾɛ́ne pθìxtɛla,ˈ bas-ṭlìya hóleˈ* His eye is open, but he is asleep (A31:6); *lɛ̀le-xəzya čù-nášaˈ bas-yắðəx hóla tlíxe ʾánna bàteˈ* Nobody has been seen, but we know that the houses have been destroyed (A29:52). Adjective omitted: *bíš m-áyya dúkθa ʾɛ̀ka xázəx?ˈ* Where could we find (something) better than this place? (A12:5). With verbs: *xáčča biš-šlèlaˈ* She became a little more calm (A4:17); *bíš madqə́rre mən-d-ó déwa ṱ-axə́lwa ʾə́rbe dìyeˈ* He (God) valued him more than the wolf that ate his sheep (A10:13).', '(2) **(not) at all**| intensifier of a negator: *y-amríwa ʾáw bíš la-mzànzərˈ yáwəl ṭéma pàyəšwaˈ* They said that it does not lose its taste at all. It keeps its taste (B10:76); *ʾáp-xa lá-biš-ile-mṣaya mqarów-əlla dìyaˈ* Nobody was able to go near her at all (A4:6); *b-qɛ̀ṭaˈ bíš liθ-məṭràθa,ˈ ʾu-bíš liθ-tàlgaˈ* In summer there are no rains at all and there is no snow at all. → *zawda, zoda*']

lemma: 'D'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**subordinating particle.**'
annotations: ['realized phonetically as *d, t, ṱ* §4.4., §10.16.']
meanings: ['(1) **annexation particle introducing nominal complements of nominals** | *brónət màlka* the son of the king (A32:21); *ṭəppəryáθət heywàneˈ* the claws of animals (A19:2); *málka d-áyya bàžər* the king of this town (A32:5); *bɛ́θa d-àw* the house of that one (A8:24); *ʾan-ʾə́rwe d-ɛ̀nila?ˈ* Whose sheep are those (A32:16); *diy-* when combined with pronominal suffixes: *bábe díye* his father (A32:31); *gu-máθa dìyənˈ* in our village (B2:6); predicative: *ʾáwwa bɛ́θa dìyəxile bráti?ˈ* Is this house yours, my daughter? (A40:13).', '(2) **relative particle introducing clausal complements of nominals** | *ʾan-suráye t-wáwa gu-Tùrkiyaˈ zílla l-ʾÌrənˈ* The Christians who were in Turkey went to Iran (B2:8); *ʾu-ʾup-báxte dìyeˈ ṱ-íle gwìrəllaˈ rába hawnàntɛlaˈ* Also his wife, whom he had married, was very clever (A17:21); *ʾɛ́-šetət mɛ́θi qəm-yawə́lla xa-bróna zòraˈ* In the year they would die he gave them a small son (A4:57); *ʾo-t-̭íle wíra ʾáw xaràmɛleˈ* The one who has entered is cursed (A23:27).', '(3) **introducing nominal and clausal complements of adverbs and prepositions** | *dáx páyəš málka šáwpət bròni?ˈ* How will he become king in place of my son? (A8:4); *qámət gə̀ppaˈ* in front of the cave (A12:7); *ʾax-d-àwwaˈ* like him (A26:34); *báθər d-ɛ̀-maθaˈ* behind that village (A24:30); *bēl-d-áyya l-d-àyyaˈ* between this and that (B5:115); *mə́ṭye l-d-o-nèraˈ* They arrived at that river (A14:58); *diy-* when combined with pronominal suffixes | *ʾax-díye* like him (A4:3); *bíye díye* with him (A14:8); *č̭ənnək̭ɛ́re díye* around him (A8:71); clausal complements: *mɛ́θən ʾax-ṱ-ila-ʾànna míθeˈ* I shall die like these people have died (A14:73); *qam-ṱ-àθiˈ mpáləṭle mən-hàbsaˈ* Before they return, release him from prison (A26:72); *m-bár t-y-óði núra gàwe,ˈ xáyəm ràbaˈ* After they put fire in it, it heats up a lot (B6:48).', '(4) **introducing clausal complements of verbs** | *ʾánna yắði ṱ-íle duglànaˈ* They know that he is a liar (A48:3); *bắyən ṱ-àzənˈ* I want to go (A8:65); *máṣəx ṱ-àmrəxˈ* We can say (B4:3).', '(5) **introducing clausal complements of clauses** | normally expressing purpose: *ʾána paqðə̀nnɛxuˈ ṱ-azítu b-ʾúrxa maṭítu ʾə̀llaˈ* I shall instruct you so that you go on the road and reach her (A8:27). → *t-la*']

lemma: 'ga'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**almost, about to; connective particle** (§15.1.1.11., §18.1.6.).'
meanings: ['(1) **almost, about to** | Combined with verb: *ga-ṱ-àθənˈ* I am about to come; *ga-máṭya ṱ-axlàleˈ* She is about to eat him (A18:26).', '(2) **connective particle** | Signalling temporal sequentiality: *rắpili m-an-képe ṱ-íla tàma,ˈ ga-maxzə́nnux ʾúrxa ṣàlətˈ* Throw me the stones that are there, then I shall show you the way down (A14:70). Introducing a comment: *lá-məre bắye xàθux.ˈ mə́re bắye Zìne.ˈ ga-ʾɛ́ni Zìneˈ ʾáxni lɛ̀ðəx.ˈ* He did not say ‘He loves your sister.’ He said ‘He loves Zine.’ Now, we do not know (by this statement) which Zine (was meant) (A26:61). At the beginning of direct speech, predominantly questions: *ʾámər ga-k̭òraˈ ʾána mò yánnux?ˈ* He said ‘Now, blind man, what can I give you?’ (A26:57); *mə́ra ga-mo-xə̀ðye b-áwwa dúša?ˈ* They said ‘Why are we so happy about this honey?’ (A14:15).']

lemma: 'ga, gaya'
grm_desc: 'n.f.'
forms: [('pl.', 'gaye, gayaθa, gaθa')]
trans: '**time, instance**'
lang: 'K.'
examples: '*málla Naṣrádin xá-ga băyéwa mbašə́lwa pàčaˈ* Once mullah Naṣradin wanted to cook pača (A5:1); *xa-xá-ga* (B6:16), *xa-xa-gáye* (B15:77), *gá-gaθa* sometimes; *b-xšàwənˈ ʾáyya quṣàrtaˈ hár gărəg-máṭe ʾəllì-xa-gaˈ* I think this cooking pot should eventually belong to me (A5:2); *tré-gaye tré wíta ʾàrbaˈ* Two times two equals four; *xámša gáye xámša wáyɛla ʾə́sri-w xàmšaˈ* Five times five is twenty-five; *raba gayaθa* many times; *ʾo-gáya qằmɛθa θélux l-kə́sliˈ* The first time you came to me ... (A1: 22). *xa-ga xeta* another time, again: *xá-ga xéta plíṭṭɛla Lelìθaˈ* Again Leliθa came out’ (A51:12); then: *bắye qaṭə̀lwale.ˈ xá-ga xéta klèleˈ* He wanted to kill him. Then he refrained (A10:3-4). *ʾɛ-ga* at that time, then | *ʾɛ́-ga zúze baṣòrewa.ˈ* At that time money was scarce (B5:5); *kút-dana ʾa-ṣə́pra mìtle,ˈ ʾɛ́-ga ʾana-mɛ̀θənˈ* If ever that sparrow dies, then I shall die (A12:41); *là-palṭət,ˈ hal-t-̭amrə́nnux plùṭgenaˈ ʾɛ̀-ga pálṭətˈ* Do not come out, until when I say to you ‘Come out!’, at *that* time you should come out (A14:67). Governing a temporal clause: *ʾɛ́-gət damə̀xwa,ˈ ṭḷaθà yomáθaˈ ʾu-ṭḷaθà lɛlăwáθa háwe dmìxaˈ* When he slept, he would be asleep for three days and three nights (A29:2). Expressing logical sequence: *ʾɛ́-ga ʾáp-ana bắyən ʾàzənˈ* So, I also want to go (A5:1). Governing a factual conditional (§19.5.8.): *ʾɛ́-gət mən-d-ánna hàwe,ˈ šúla bṱ-ázəl la-qàma!ˈ* If there are these (gold pieces), the job will go ahead! (A4:15).'

lemma: 'hal, ha-'
grm_desc: 'prep.'
trans: '**until, up to; before; until when.**'
annotations: ['§13.3.10., §19.3.9.']
meanings: ['(1) **until, up to** | *hal-ʾaṣə́rta plìxɛleˈ* He worked until evening (A16:5); *ʾo-mənnɛ́xu t-dàqərˈ b-Mằmo,ˈ m-áxxa hál qaṣrət-mìraˈ ṱ-oðə́xle də̀mmaˈ* Whoever of you touches Mămo, we shall scatter his blood from here until the palace (A26:68); *yáʿni xamšá daqíqela hal-ʾə̀ṣraˈ ʾáti ʾàθetiˈ* after five or ten minutes you should come back (A22:22); *hal-ʾìman ṱ-áwət hátxa mdagóle?ˈ* For how long will you lie like this? (A26:56). Before a prepositional phrase: *wíyəx pláša m-ʾaṣə́rta hal-gu-mbadlàθaˈ* We fought from evening until morning (A12:19); *hal-gu-réšət ṭúra* up to the top of the mountain (A14:49). Combined with connective particle *w*: *m-ó-yoma dwíqəlle Mắmo gu-hàbsa,ˈ ʾu-hàl-ʾədyoˈ* From that day he has held Mămo in prison, until today (A26:75); *kùllən,ˈ mən-yále zóre ʾu-hal-gòṛeˈ* all of us, from young children to old people (B16:4). Content clause as complement (often shortened to *ha-*): *zílela hal-mə́ṭyela l-qàṣraˈ* They went until they arrived at the palace (A24:49); *kazíwa práməlla har-palṭìwa,ˈ hál plíṭla hàtxaˈ* They tried to cut them down, but they kept growing up, until they grew like this (A38:15); *mxéla l-ġðàðeˈ ha-t-ṭḷáθna mìtlaˈ* They beat one another until the three of them died (A22:35).', '(2) **before** | *ha-ṱ-íle ʾə̀θya,ˈ mpuláṭṭɛla fằqihˈ* Before he came back, she took out the jurist (A22:39); *pɛšáwa tàlga hal-qedámtaˈ* It would become ice before morning (B15:26).', '(3) **until when** | *là-palṭət,ˈ hal-ṱ-amrə́nnux plùṭgenaˈ ʾɛ̀-ga pálṭətˈ* Do not come out, until when I say to you ‘Come out!’, at that time you should come out (A14:67).']

lemma: 'har'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**always; again; still; as soon as; directly; just, only; the same; surely** (§15.11.).'
lang: 'K.'
meanings: ['(1) **always, constantly** | *har-bxàya-wawaˈ* They were constantly continued crying (A25:5); *ʾu-ʾáti har-háwət baràyeˈ ʾu-sáprət ku-t-áθe làxxaˈ* You be outside all the time and wait for whoever comes here (A22:23); *har-blígət b-kàsuxˈ* You are always busy with your stomach (A23:10).', '(2) **again** | *yómət ṭḷàθaˈ har-ṣlèlaˈ* On the third day she went down again (A22:18).', '(3) **still** | Temporal persistence: *ʾu-dəbbóre hár-hola qam-tắrət bòyaˈ* The hornets were still before the door of the hole (A20:9); *har-xáθe ʾi-bằyelaˈ* He still loves his sister (A18:16); *ʾáy har-là-yawəllaˈ* It still does not give it back (A34:4); *hal-lɛle* < *har-lɛle*: *hal-lɛ̀la gláyaˈ* She (the mother) still does not reveal (the truth) (A38:6). Logically unexpected: *kəmə̀t ṱ-árqenaˈ tópe har-ṭapyàliˈ* However much I run, a gun will still reach me (B9:3).', '(4) **as soon as** | *har-ðìlɛxu príqlən mən-ṭúra,ˈ dɛ́rən tòpe,ˈ kút-xa maxèlaˈ xánjər dìye,ˈ ʾo-ṱ-íle qáme díye qaṭə̀lleˈ* As soon as you know that we have finished (coming over) the mountain, I shall fire a gun and everyone will strike with his dagger and kill the man in front of him (B19:6); *har-qítla bìyux,ˈ qaṭlílux ṱ-axlìluxˈ* As soon as they hit you, they will kill you and eat you (A22:39).', '(5) **directly** | *har-ʾə́θyɛle mən-ṭúra réša-reša d-o-gàreˈ* He came straight from the mountain onto the roof (A23:14).', '(6) **just, only** | *har-ʾàna hon-zlímaˈ* Only I am wronged (A13:5); *lá har-ʾáxni zlìmeˈ* Not only we are wronged (A13:16); *har-ʾàwwɛleˈ* He is alone (A17:16); *har-ʾàtiˈ* you yourself (and nobody else) (A27:6); *hár-xa xále dìyeleˈ* It is his one and only uncle (A28:11). Narrowing the extent of an action: *ʾína bróna lɛ̀la xíltəlle.ˈ har-nobáltəlle muttɛ́θəlle mattòye.ˈ* She did not eat the boy. She just took him and put him down. (A19:7); *ʾána har-ṣálən mðìtaˈ mɛ́θən ʾixàlaˈ ʾu-ʾàθenaˈ* I’ll just go down to the town to bring food and come back (A26:30).', '(7) **the same** | in combination with demonstratives: *hàr ʾo-yóma* on the same day (A25:4).', '(8) **surely, indeed** | *ʾáxni har-xònən-itˈ* You are indeed our brother (A39:12); *ʾay-xá-yoma har-t-yằðaˈ ṱ-íle míθa brònənˈ* She will surely know one day that our son is dead (A4:39)']

lemma: 'heš, həš, š'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**still; (not) yet; (no) longer** (§15.10.).'
meanings: ['(1) **still** | *héš xúya xùyɛleˈ* It is still very dark (A30:36); *ʾáy heš-hóla gu-gòmaˈ* She is still in the basement stable (A18:22). As an intensifier of a comparative: *heš-bìš qam-xóna díya qímtɛlaˈ* She rose still earlier than her brother (A8:69); *b-qáryən ʾu-hèš-biš záwdaˈ* I shall call yet louder (A8:72).', '(2) *heš* + negator = **not yet** | *heš-lɛ́le làxxaˈ* He is not here yet; *heš-lɛ́le ʾə̀θyaˈ* He has not come yet; *š-lɛ́wa mšúrya xála gə̀llaˈ* It had not yet started to eat grass (B5:175); *qəm-dári ʾan-dáwwe heš-t-là brázaˈ* They have poured out the *dawwe* while it is not yet dry (B14:1).', '(3) *la* + *heš* (generally contracted to *leš, lɛš, laš, ləš*) = **no longer** | *léš-ʾaθəx hayorə̀xluxˈ* We shall no longer come to help you (A48:6); *leš faydáləx qáṭlət gànəxˈ* It will no longer be of any use to you to kill yourself (A38:16); *ʾáqlət susɛ́xu ʾən-píšla kèpa,ˈ léš maṣítu jawjìtuˈ* If the legs of your horses have become stone, you will no longer be able to move (A8:28); *léš-ile gu-bɛ̀θaˈ* He is no longer in the house; *lɛ́š-in xzàyaˈ* I can no longer see (A24:2).']

meanings: ['(1) **how many? how much?** (interrogative) | *ʾína kəmà-gaye zíllux ʾu-šqíllux ʾáyya?ˈ* How many times have you gone and taken it? (B15:90); *ʾawwa ʾaskaríya dìyeˈ ṭlà-kəma dánɛla?ˈ* For what time is this army of his for? Used independently: *kəmà t-yátli?ˈ* How much will you give me? (A24:5). Used predicatively: *sáʾət kəmɛ̀la?ˈ* The time is how much? (= What time is it?) (A26:27). Adverb: *kəmà zonə́tle?ˈ* For how much will you buy him? (A24:23).', '(2) **some, several** | *kə́ma gàyeˈ* several times (B9:18); *y-oráwa kə́ma yàrxeˈ* Several months passed (B5:18).', '(3) **so much, so many** (exclamatory) | *ʾána kəmà dána ṱ-in-mṣalóye ṭla-márya ʾàlahaˈ ta-t-yawə́lli ʾə̀mma dáweˈ* I was praying to the Lord God so many times to give me a hundred gold coins (A6:10); *kəma-basìmtɛla ʾixála!ˈ* The food is so delicious! (A21:31). Adverb: *baxtáθa kə́ma zădíwa mən-xuwwàwe!ˈ* The women feared snakes so much! (B5:78). Governing a clause (usually abbreviated to *ma*): *ʾánna ma-ṱ-íla xmíle b-ġðàðe!ˈ* How happy they were together! (A4:50); *ʾu-ṭə̀lyelaˈ ma-t-wáwa kčìxeˈ* They slept, so tired were they (A14:43).', '(4) **however much, as much as** (governing a clause) | *kəmə̀t ṱ-árqenaˈ tópe har-ṭapyàliˈ* However much I run, a gun will still reach me (B9:3); *xúl kəma-t-bằyətˈ* Eat as much as you want (B15:56).', '(5) **when** | *ma-t-wéwa brōn-málka qə́ryəlle ʾo-kθàwa,ˈ mə́re spày!ˈ* When the son of the king had read the letter, he said ‘Good!’ (A11:18).', '(6) **as for** | *kəmá ṱ-íle Rùstam,ˈ ʾáw mbaqórəlle Tătár-i Slemán-i Sə̀ndiˈ* As for Rustam, he asked for Tătar-i Sleman-i Səndi (A28:24).']

lemma: 'l-'
grm_desc: 'prep.'
trans: '**to, for, upon, at, by:** Admominal uses'
annotations: ['with pronominal suffixes: *le, ʾəlle*', '§13.3.12., §16.2.']
meanings: ['(1) Destination: *si-dúṛ l-šòpuxˈ* Go back to your place (A15:20).', '(2) Objective without movement: *ʾálaha šuxa-l-šə́mme* God—praise be to his name (A6:10).', '(3) **upon**: *hóle tíwa l-kèpaˈ* He is sitting on a stone (A15:13); occasionally with the form *ʾal-*: *ʾal-ʾằraˈ* on the ground (A21:5).', '(4) General spatial location: *hóle ʾàryaˈ l-àyya gótaˈ ʾu-ʾə̀zzaˈ hóla l-àyya gótaˈ* There is lion on this side and a she-goat on the other side (A24:15); *hóla spára l-kàweˈ* They are waiting at the window (A4:59).', '(5) Expression of the agent: *šáwwaθna hóla xíle l-dèwaˈ* The seven of them have been eaten by wolves (A23:15).', '(6) Combined with other prepositions: *ʾo-gáya qằmɛθa θélux l-kə́sliˈ* The first time you came to me (A1:22). Use of *l-* + pronominal suffixes:', '(1) Inflection of past verbal base: *qṭille* He killed (him), *zille* He went.', '(2) Direct and indirect object: *qaṭəlle* He kills him; *hawəlle* He gives to him.', '(3) Possession: *ʾitli kθawa* I have a book. Use of *ʾəll-* + pronominal suffix:', '(1) Destination: *ʾə́θyela mə́ṭye ʾə̀lleˈ* They came up to him (A7:19);', '(2) Direction (without movement), beneficiary: *ʾámər ʾə́lla dìyaˈ* He says to her (A16:7); *wídla fṭárta ʾə̀lliˈ* She made me breakfast (A21:38).', '(3) on (surface): *mattí ʾíða ʾə̀lleˈ* They place a hand on it (B5:100); *qímle murə́sle hátxa míya ʾəllèyˈ* He sprinkled water on them like this (B6:11).', '(4) over (abstract relation): *hótu pšàma ʾə́lla díyaˈ* You are sad over it (A5:10).', '(5) direct object (bound to verb): *múttətəlle* You put him (A22:39); *prìmənəlla* I cut it (f.) (A22:9).']

lemma: 'la'
grm_desc: 'n.f.'
trans: '**side, direction**'
lang: 'K.'
examples: '*ṣə̀lyelaˈ swánət ʾúmra la-qámθa díya ràmta-wawaˈ* They (the sheep) went down over the eaves of the church, the front side of which was high (B18:6). Used mainly in adverbial expressions: *la-qáma* forwards; *la-bára* backwards; *kú mənná ṱ-íle pláṭa mən-gawàye,ˈ pláṭa la-qam-tằraˈ* Each one who goes out from inside, going towards the outside (B11:8); *y-azíwa la-zràqət yómaˈ* They would go in the direction of the rising of the sun (A8:22); *hóle ʾə́θya Déwa Zàrˈ ... m-la-gnay-yòmaˈ* Dewa Zar has come ... from the West (A28:14); *ʾɛ́we ʾən-θéla m-la-Zàwa,ˈ ṱ-áθe xa-yóma ṭàwaˈ* If the clouds come from the side of the Zab (i.e. the East), a good day will come (D2:16); *hola θela m-la-Maye* Look she has come from the direction of Maye (C2:46).'

lemma: 'la'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**no** (variants *laʾ, laʾa*)**, not; neither/nor; asseverative particle.**'
meanings: ['(1) **no** | *mə́ra làˈ ʾáti ṣli-be-màlkaˈ* They said ‘No, you go down to the house of the king’ (A25:87); *mə́re bráti lá là!ˈ* He said ‘My daughter, no, no!’ (A21:30); *mə́re làʾ!ˈ* He said ‘No!’ (A1:6); *ʾámər làʾa!ˈ* He says ‘No!’ (A21:42).', '(2) **not** | *la-ṣábrəx ṱ-òrəxˈ* We do not dare enter (A14:40); *lə́mu la-qìmlux?ˈ* Why did you not stand? (A26:48); *bróni là qəṭlúle!ˈ* Do not kill my son! (A33:6); *ʾána lɛ̀-gorən,ˈ la-ʾàti gáwrətˈ* I shall not marry, so long as you do not marry (A25:83); *ʾáni maṣlə́xwa ʾə̀rxe,ˈ ṭaxnə̀xwala,ˈ là kúlla nášeˈ bas-ʾàxniˈ* ‘We brought them down to the water-mill and ground them, not everybody, but we did (this) (B10:88). Negating an adjective: *fə́lfəl ... là-xšilta* uncrushed pepper (B10:21).', '(3) *la ... la* **neither ... nor** | *ʾána làn dmíxa,ˈ là-b-lele,ˈ là-b-yomaˈ* I have not slept, neither at night nor during the day (A24:24); *ʾána lànwa wíðaˈ là xarbayúθaˈ là spayúθa ṭla-čú-našaˈ* I have done neither evil nor good to anybody (A14:23); *lá-băyəx la-mìyaˈ ʾu-la-čù-məndiˈ* We want neither water nor anything else (A39:12).', '(4) **asseverative particle** | *la-hóle mìθaˈ* He is indeed dead (A17:2); A: *štélux čàyux?ˈ* B: *la-štèli!* A: Have you drunk your tea? lemma: 'ləbba'
grm_desc: 'n.m.'
forms: [('pl.', 'ləbbe')]
trans: '**heart; kernel of fruit or berry**'
examples: 'Idioms: *yawa ləbba l-* to console (after death), to encourage: *híwɛle lə́bba ṭla-gʸáne dìyeˈ* He took heart (A8:58). *ləbbi zille l-d-ɛ qumta* I fainted at the sight of that figure (C2:55). *bəd-lə́bba gu-bɛ́θət bába dìyɛlaˈ* She thinks that she is in her father’s house (A21:18). *gu-lə́bbe díye mtuxmə̀nneˈ* I thought to himself (A39:5). *lə́bbe biyáxu tlìqetuˈ* He thinks you are lost (A14:85). *dwiqále b-lə̀bbeˈ* He kept it in mind. *ʾáyya quṣárta ràba šapirta,ˈ rába zála ləbbì-ʾəllaˈ* This cooking pot is very nice, I like it a lot (A5:2); *hóle zála lə̀bbiˈ ṱ-ásqət ṣɛ́dət ʾə́rbət wàlaˈ* I would like you to go up and hunt for wild sheep (A26:44). *lə́bbi basìmaˈ* I am happy. *ʾáwwa náša lə́bbe pqìleˈ* The heart of that burst (= He was terrified) (A32:2). *qìdle lə́bbi,ˈ xóni zòra-wewaˈ* My heart yearned (for him), he was my young brother (A34:24); *mən-lə́bbe díye qìða,ˈ dɛ́re xɛ̀la,ˈ načə̀lle ʾo-šəryóxaˈ* Out of his fervour, he applied force and pulled the tether apart (A28:20). *xílli lə̀bbuxˈ* My dear, you are dear to me (A39:12). *ʾána hóle píša lə̀bbiˈ* I am angry. *t-la-páyəš lə́bbən b-ġðàðeˈ* so that we do not feel anger at each other (B5:10); *ṭḷàθnaˈ xonăwáθət Qára Tèždinˈ mopíšəlle ləbbèyˈ* The three brothers of Qara Teždin became angry (A26:71). *ʾánna píšla gu-lə́bbe díye kùllaˈ* All these (words) weighed on his heart (A38:13). *ʾáyya lɛ̀ða,ˈ lə́bba ṣə̀pya žáreˈ* She did not know, she was innocent, poor thing (A14:99). *hátxa baṣlóṣe gu-lə́bbət nàšaˈ* (They) glow in the heart of man (= they captivate one’s heart) (A8:16). *m-kúlla lə́bbi bắyən ʾána qaṭlìtuliˈ* With all my heart I want you to kill me (B9:14).'

lemma: 'liθ'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**negative existential particle** (§8.20.1., §15.3.8., §17.3.)'
annotations: ['variants: *liθən, liθena, liθga, liθgən, liθgena*. past: *liθwa*']
meanings: ['(1) Used without suffixes | *líθ čù-məndiˈ* There is nothing (A21:5); *líθ ʾáp-xa gu-bɛ̀θa?ˈ* Is there nobody in the house? (A22:32); *čú-qala líθən mənnèyˈ* There is no sound of them (A18:15); *ʾɛ́-ga líθwa bə̀rqaˈ* At that time there was not electricity (B10:45); *líθwa qá-t mbaqríwa bràtaˈ* It was not the practice to ask the girl (B5:2). Used interrogatively to draw attention to a particular point: *ʾo-šúla ʾáwwa y-amrə́xwale qə̀rṭa líθən?ˈ* We called this job trimming, you see (B5:141).', '(2) With L-suffixes expressing possession: *ʾána zúza lìtliˈ* I do not have money. (A22:19); *lítle la-bába la-yə́mma la-ʾàp-xaˈ* He does not have a father, a mother or anybody (A17:17); *lìθwale quṣə̀rtaˈ* He did not have a cooking-pot (A5:1); *lítla xàmˈ* That’s fine, no problem.']

lemma: 'ma'
grm_desc: 'part. pron.'
trans: '**what?** (§7.5., §14.9.13.)'
examples: '*xúwwe mà ṱ-áwəð b-an-álpa dáwe?ˈ* What will the snake do with those thousand gold coins? (A1:8); *xáθi mà-ləx?ˈ* Sister, what is the matter with you? (A34:12); *mà-lux zə́dya?ˈ* Why are you afraid? (A11:6); *má-lux mə́nne ʾàti?ˈ* What business is it of yours? (A32:3); *ʾána má-li mə̀nnux?ˈ* What have I to do with you? (A32:22); *má-ləx bráta ṱ-it-hátxa bxàyaˈ* What is the matter with you girl that you are weeping so much? (A34:20); *sállət míya yắðət mɛ̀la?ˈ* (< *mà-ila*) Do you know what a basket of water is? (A16:10). Modifier of a noun: *ʾánna ma-brinànela gu-réšuxˈ* What wounds are these on your head? (A29:6). Exclamatory modifier of a noun: *ʾu-Bə́lbəl Hazár yăðátla ma-báxta xàmθɛlaˈ* You know what a beautiful woman Bəlbəl Hazar is (A8:65). Expressing an exclamatory proposition: *ma-píštət k̭awə̀lla!ˈ* How you have become a ruin! (A18:16). With remonstrating force in negated questions *ma-lat-ðáya b-gánəx qàrθɛla?ˈ* Don’t you know yourself that it is cold?! (A20:1). Before imperatives: *ma-yəmmi pɛli zwaðe* Mother, bake me supplies! (A50:9). Before a repeated noun to express a more general class (§14.11.): *jawə́tta ṭla-pràmaˈ ʾanna qɛ́se ma-qɛ̀seˈ* A chopper was for chopping wood and the like (B5:141).'

meanings: ['(1) Separation or removal: *šqíləlla mən-d-ɛ-dɛ̀rtaˈ* They took it from that enclosure (A15:12); *nìxlən m-Čúxoˈ* We are relieved of Čuxo (A7:19).', '(2) Source or origin: *ʾən-kʸálo m-gu-màθa,ˈ čɛrxìwala máθaˈ xáṣə dawɛ̀reˈ* If the bride was from the village, they would take her round the village on the back of mules (B10:34).', '(3) Temporal starting point: *ʾu-hóla mšuyðánta mən-d-ó-yoma ṱ-íla xzíθəlle ʾàwˈ* She has been mad from the day that she saw him (A4:12).', '(4) Partitive: *šqíltɛla mən-dàweˈ* She took some of the gold coins (A10:7).', '(5) Comparison: *ʾína mástət ʾə́rwe rába biš-basimtɛ́la biš-príštɛla mən-d-a-t-tàwreˈ* But the yoghurt of sheep is much better and more choice than that of cattle (B5:173).', '(6) Cause: *ʾána-ži m-kɛ́rbi ʾə́θyən ʾá-kθɛθa múttənna rəš-núra ʾu-xìlənnaˈ* I, out of my anger, came and put the chicken on the fire and ate it (A2:11).', '(7) Material: *məlxáwa ʾíwa mtúrṣa m-qɛ̀saˈ* The winnowing fork was made from wood (B5:87).', '(8) Stative spatial location: *ʾasṛíwala b-qɛ́sa ʾu-m-áy-gota qɛ̀saˈ ʾu-m-áy-gota qɛ̀saˈ* They would bind them to a stick, with a stick this side and a stick that side (B7:16).', '(9) Comitative: *mən-xuráne díye píšɛle gu-ṭúra xá-yoma yóme trèˈ* With his friends he remained in the mountains one or two days (A4:2).', '(10) Combined with other prepositions: *ʾu-ṭríðəlle m-gu-bɛ̀θaˈ* He drove him from the house (A16:11); *xa-qála ʾáθe m-qam-tắrət bɛ̀θaˈ* A voice came from before the house (A22:29); *ʾázən šáqlən zùziˈ m-rəš-ʾɛ̀naˈ* I shall go to take my money from on top of the spring (A15:2).']

lemma: 'mo, mu, modi, maw, mawdi'
grm_desc: 'part. pron.'
trans: '**what; why?; how could it be? how (exclamatory).**'
annotations: ['§7.5., §14.9.12., §17.1.4., §17.7.13., §19.1.2.4., §19.2.2.']
meanings: ['(1) **what** | Interrogative: *mò-băyət?ˈ* What do you want? (A13:13); *mòdi wídle?ˈ* What did he do? (A25:19); *mú bṱ-àwe?!ˈ* What will it be? (= That is fine, OK) (A18:33); *mo-ʾìba?!* What is there in it?! (= That is fine, OK) (A13:1); *màw-lux?ˈ* What is the matter with you? (A31:9); *mút qála dìyi?ˈ* What is my voice? (A25:44). Indirect question: *xáze mòdila qə́ṣṣətˈ* He sees what the problem is (A22:43); *làn-ðaʾa mo-qaríwaleˈ* I do not know what they call him (A12:20); *ṱ-ázən xázən mòdi píše ʾan-nášeˈ* I shall go to see what has become of those people (A18:12). Modifier of a noun: *ʾáwwa mò-tăhər nášɛle?ˈ* What kind of man is he? (A25:31); *ʾáyya mòdi mðítɛla?ˈ* What town is this? (A26:26). Exclamatory: *ʾína mù-brata!ˈ* But what a girl! (A13:11). Head of a relative clause: *mšaróyela kθàwaˈ bɛθwáθət nàšeˈ ʾu-mo-ṱ-itlèyˈ* They start registering the houses of people and what they have (B1:16).', '(2) **why?** | *mu-ṣṭímlux bɛ̀θi?ˈ* Why have you ruined me? (literally: Why have you destroyed my house?) (A15:14); *mút ʾáti tíwta làxxa?ˈ* Why are you sitting here? (A25:58); *módit ʾə̀θya?ˈ* Why have you come? (A17:31).', '(3) **how could it be?** | questioning possibility of sth., mainly with short forms *mu-, mut*: *ʾánna šáwwa yamàθaˈ ʾana mù pɛðə́nna?ˈ* How could I cross these seven seas? (A12:26); *mùt hole-pč̣íla?ˈ* How could it be that it is crooked? (A17:20); *mut-yằðən ʾɛ́kɛla?ˈ* How shall I know where she is? (A14:98).', '(4) **how (exclamatory)** | Before a verb: *téla mo-ṭréle ʾə̀lla!ˈ* How the fox ran to it! (A49:4).']

lemma: 'qam'
grm_desc: 'prep.'
trans: '**before (spatial and temporal); in (adversity), from (adversity); on account of (adversity); instead of.**'
annotations: ['with pronominal suffixes: *qame*', '§13.3.16.']
meanings: ['(1) **before (spatial)** | *qam-ʾɛ́nuxˈ* before your eyes (A15:15). Obstacle: *muttɛ́θətwa qámi xa-ṭúrət skinyàθaˈ* You had placed before me a mountain of knives (A24:33), *hálli xá-məndi ṱ-àxlənˈ t-lá-pɛšən kə́twa qam-ʾàqluxˈ* Give me something to eat so that I am not a thorn in your foot (A26:57). Duty: *ʾána ʾíθ šùla qámiˈ* I have a job to do (A24:45). Outside: *qam-tăra* outside the door (of the house), *qámət gə̀ppaˈ* outside the cave (A12:7). After verbs of movement: *ṱ-azítu qam-d-o-gə̀ppaˈ* You should go to the cave (A8:28), *zíla, zíla zìla,ˈ qam-xákma ṭuràneˈ rába ràmeˈ* He went a long way (and came) to some very high mountains (A14:66). At the disposal of, for the benefit of: *ʾáyya dəkkána qàməxˈ* This shop is for you (to choose from as you wish) (A22:20); *ʾáni daríwala qam-qənyàneˈ* They would put them out for the animals (to eat) (B15:50). Leading animals: *xa-šăvána ... y-azə́lwa qam-ʾə̀rweˈ* A shepherd used to go to look after sheep (A10:1), *qu-sí qam-ʾə̀rwe!ˈ* Go and look after the sheep! (A10:5). In charge of: *ṭaxána qam-ðà-ʾarxeˈ* a miller in charge of a water-mill (A32:1).', '(2) **before (temporal)** | with a nominal: *qám šáwwi tmáni šə̀nne* seventy or eighty years ago (B5:179); *qam-dànaˈ* beforehand (A4:30); *qam-mxɛ́θət madə̀nxaˈ* before the rise of dawn (A8:51); *ʾáw qam-mə̀nnux hóle ʾə́θya láxxaˈ* He has come back here before you (A22:39). With a clause complement: *qam-ṱ-àθiˈ mpáləṭle mən-hàbsaˈ* Before they return, release him from prison (A26:72).', '(3) **in (adversity)** | *ʾup-ʾàniˈ náše ʾi-xawšìwalaˈ mattíwale gu-gòmeˈ qá-t barzìwa,ˈ qa-t-là-hawiwa qam-mə́ṭraˈ* People would store these (pieces of wood) and put them in the basement to dry, so that they would not be in the rain (B15:19); *ʾəθyewəx kope kope qam-məṭra ʾu-qam dalope* We have come bending down in rain and drizzle (C1:14); *maqðánnux qam-šmàyyaˈ* I shall burn you in the sun (A12:31).', '(4) **from (adversity)** | In contexts expressing escaping from or sheltering from: *ríqən qam-màmiˈ* I have run away from my paternal uncle (A25:42); *lɛ́ka b-šárṭət qam-ʾiθàθi?ˈ* Where can you escape from my hands? (A28:21); *mṭášət qam-Lelìθaˈ* Hide from Leliθa (A51:6); *mṭošéle qam-tàlgaˈ* He sheltered from the snow (A28:3).', '(5) **on account of (adversity)** | *ʾáskar kúlla mìtlaˈ qam-qàleˈ* All the army died on account of his voice (A52:13); *šəlmanā̀tˈ dìplaˈ qam-xɛ̀laˈ* The bars have bent due to the force (put on them) (A52:9); *kšíple bɛ́θa qam-tàlgaˈ* The house collapsed on account of the snow; *tréle qam-mə̀ṭraˈ* He was soaked on account of the rain.', '(6) **instead of** | *ʾɛ́-ga qam-lámpa ʾíθwa šràʾaˈ* At that time instead of an (electric) lamp there was an (oil) lamp (A33:1).']

lemma: 'qama qama'

lang: 'K./A.'
meanings: ['(1) **condition** | *ʾaláha hole-mìraˈ t-yawə̀lluxˈ b-šàrṭˈ kú-mdit yawə̀lluxˈ ta-šwáwux t-yáwəl trèˈ* God has said that he will give to you on condition that everything he gives to you he will give to your neighbour twofold (A3:4); *šŭrūṭ-díyi mkumlìlux?ˈ* Have you fulfilled my conditions? (A12:16); *ha-t-dóqət šárṭ mən-d-òˈ nàšaˈ* until you agree on conditions with that man (A12:42).', '(2) **agreement** | *wídle šàrṭˈ ta-máxa l-ġðàðeˈ* He made an agreement that they would strike each other (in a contest) (A52:15).', '(3) **test, ordeal, challenge** | *ʾən-šắrəṭ díyi qəm-yăðə̀tla,ˈ xo-b-gawrànnuxˈ* If you know (the answer to) my test, I shall indeed marry you (A25:62).', '(4) **court case** | *ʾitléy šăráṭe ṱ-amríla qa-màlkaˈ* They have cases (to present) to the king (A17:31).', '(5) **judgement, sentence** | *šárṭ qázi t-yawə́lla ṭlàluxˈ* The judge will make a sentence in your favour (A6:7).', '(6) **court (proceedings)** | *wírela šarṭ-qàziˈ* They entered the court of the judge (A6:9).', '(7) **custom** | *w-áxni lìθ gu-šắrəṭ dìyənˈ bràtaˈ krəstyàntaˈ gáwra mušəlmànaˈ* But it is not our custom that a Christian girl marries a Muslim (B4:9).']

lemma: 'tama'
grm_desc: 'adv.'
trans: '**there**'
examples: 'Used to refer anaphorically to a location out of sight of speech situation: *bálki lá-hawe tàmaˈ* Perhaps he will not be there (A1:10); *sab-ɛ́-ga xúrme lìθwa támaˈ* since at that time there were no dates there (in Barwar) (B5:12); *táxtɛla mútte hàtxaˈ ta-ṣáli tàmaˈ* They have put a board like this in order to go down there (A22:10). Repeated to express movement: *ʾan-tre-maláxe ... θéla pyáða táma tàmaˈ* Those two angels ... came passing by (A4:44); *ʾáw brōn-málka θéle jwája tam-tàmaˈ* The son of the king came walking along there (A8:14). Temporal sense in expression *m-tama hodəx* from then onwards, afterwards: *xárθa m-táma hòdəx,ˈ xɛ̀riˈ ʾína bɛ́θe díye kúlle qìðaˈ* Then, afterwards they look and see that all his house had burnt down (A48:7).'

lemma: 'tămaha'

trans: '**over there (in sight)**'
examples: '*də́ryəlla gu-qaṣxàneˈ ʾu-múttəlla tămàhaˈ* He put them (the bones) in the pan and put it aside (A2:5); *hóle xa-šoramíṭa m-áxxa l-tămàhaˈ dmíxa kə́sla dìyaˈ* A giant from here to there (in size) is lying with her (A4:52).'

(A31:2); *ʾámər xáṭər ʾalàha,ˈ ʾu-xáṭər mšìxa,ˈ bas-lá dáqrət bìyiˈ* For the sake of God and the Messiah, do not touch me (A15:21); *xáṭər xaṭrànaˈ* for the sake of respect (B5:10); *bəd-xáṭər d-ó-xona zòraˈ* for the sake of that young brother (A12:22).']

lemma: 'xo, xoθ-'
grm_desc: 'prep.'
trans: '**under**'
annotations: ['with pronominal suffixes: *xoθe*', '§13.3.23.']
examples: '*múttəlla xo-kosìθeˈ* He put them under his hat (A23:6), *tfíqla dàwe xo-ʾáqla díyaˈ* She found gold coins under her leg (A10:7); *dɛ́rət ʾíðux xo-d-ò-kepaˈ* Put your hand under that stone (A12:27); *xo-qðala maxmore* with jewels (hanging down) under her neck (C6:4); *ʾáxni xoθ-tagbártət màlkəxˈ* We are under the administration of the king (A8:80). After verbs of movement: *y-aθɛ́wa xo-túθa \ue001č̣ùwaˈ* They would come under the smooth mulberry tree (B5:203), *kú ṱ-íle ṣláya xo-qárše ʾə̀ltəx,ˈ pyáša dàwaˈ* Everything that fell down under the beams became gold (A10:11), *mṭeli xo-Dwile* I arrived under (the village of) Dwile (C2:30). Combined with *mən* expressing static location: *ʾu-m-xòθeˈ y-oðíwa nùraˈ* Then under it they would put fire (B5:183). Expressing movement: *másta plíṭla m-xóθa dìyaˈ* The yoghurt came out from underneath it (A30:21).'

lemma: 'xo-, xu-'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**intensifying particle** (§17.9.2.)'
examples: 'Intensifying negation with remonstrating force: *xo-la-mɛ́θən làxxaˈ* I shall not die here (A20:11); *yába ʾan-ʾə́mma dàwe,ˈ xu-là mbaqrə̀təlliˈ* Well, do not ask me about those hundred gold coins (A14:65); *xu-lanwa-mírəllux maxzə́tli xăzìnaˈ* I had not told you to show me a treasure (A14:23). In negative questions, usually remonstrating: *xo-lat-mírta xà-məndi?ˈ* Did you not say something? (= surely you said something?) (A26:34); *bábi tə́mməl ʾáyya mðíta xu-kùmta-wawa?ˈ* Father, was this town not black yesterday? (= surely this town was black yesterday) (A4:35). In positive questions: *gúrzə šə́rmux xo-ʾána ṱ-azə́nwa bìya?ˈ* Would I be finished off by your stupid club (literally: the club of your behind)?! (A52:17). Introducing apodosis: *ʾən-šắrəṭ díyi qəm-yăðə̀tla,ˈ xo-b-gawrànnuxˈ* If you know (the answer to) my challenge, I shall indeed marry you’ (A25:62); *ʾən-θèliˈ xó bàxtiwətˈ* If I come back, then you are my wife (A25:66).'

lemma: 'xoð-'
grm_desc: 'pron.'
trans: '**pronoun of isolation** (§14.6.)'
examples: '*xòðiwənˈ* I am alone (A22:32); *pìšelaˈ har-ʾàni-tre l-xoðéyˈ* Only those two remained by themselves (A20:9); *ʾáw xa-l-xóðe díye tămàhaˈ* He is all alone there (A27:5).'

lemma: 'zawda, zoda'
grm_desc: 'part.'
trans: '**more (quantity), too much** (§14.8.2.)'
annotations: ['often combined with *biš*: *biz-zawda/biz-zoda, bi-zawda/bi-zoda*']
examples: 'Expressing an increase in quantity: *xá-saʿat biz-zòdaˈ* one hour more (B5:54); *mə́ndi zàwdaˈ* something more (A3:1); *kùl-məndi bi-záwdaˈ* more of everything (A3:3). In estimates of quantity: *ʾəštà yarxéˈ xamšà yarxéˈ biz-zàwdaˈ* five or six months, or more (B5:3). More than: *ʾu-bréle díya b-xšáwən biz-záwda mən-ʾəč̣č̣á-mma ʾálpa nàšeˈ* By now there have been born, I think, more than nine-hundred thousand people (B2:10); *záwda mən-ʾarbá-mma šə̀nneleˈ* It is more than four hundred years old (B6:31); *ʾáxni be-Tòməxˈ lá-maxəx zóda l-xàˈ* We the family of Toma do not strike more than one (blow) (A52:24). Excessive quantity: *zàwdɛla mə́nniˈ* It is too much for me (to tell) (A26:65). With adverbs: *lá maspərə́xləx bi-zàwdaˈ* We shall not make you wait any more (A4:42); *xắyiwa biz-zàwdaˈ* They survived longer (B5:190). In combination *sama zawda/zoda* expressing the majority of a set: *xákma har-damxíwa l-ằraˈ ʾap-áni gàre.ˈ ʾína sáma zóda ʾiyɛ́wala qaràwət.ˈ* Some would even sleep on the floor of the roof. Most people, however, had a bed. (B5:204); *ʾína sáma zòdaˈ y-oðíwa ʾằraqˈ* Most people, however, would make arak (B5:213). Idiom: *mìr-e-mənˈ zàwdɛla mə́nni,ˈ ʾána ṱ-amrənnɛ̀xuˈ mšáxəlpu dukàneˈ* My lord, may I humbly suggest you change places (Literally: It is too much for me, let me say to you, change places) (A26:65).'

examples: '*bas-ʾána zodànta-llɛxuˈ quṣárta mə́nni t-muθéli llɛ̀xuˈ* But the cooking pot that I have brought you is an extra one for you (A5:6).'

They ate and drank. (A7:3). Adversative when in negative clause: *ʾó-yōm ṱ-ìle plíṭaˈ bróne díye mìθɛle.ˈ ʾu-ʾáxni-ži láx muqíme m-báθre díye màlkaˈ* On the day he left, his son died.
